# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Java Annotation Processing for Kafka Config Keys

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that use the @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef annotation pattern for configuration documentation: the annotation definitions, the config documentation generator, and the AbstractConfig subclasses that use annotated config keys.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Summary

I found **46 Java source files** using the **ConfigDef and ConfigKey pattern** for configuration documentation in Apache Kafka. This isn't actually an annotation pattern (`@interface`), but rather a powerful class-based pattern for declarative configuration definition.

### Key Findings:

**Core Framework (2 files):**
- `ConfigDef.java` - Main configuration schema definition class
- `AbstractConfig.java` - Base class for all configuration classes

**Configuration Classes (25+ files):**
- Client configs: ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig, AdminClientConfig
- Streams configs: StreamsConfig, TopologyConfig
- Connect configs: ConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, SourceConnectorConfig, WorkerConfig, TaskConfig, and various converters
- Mirror configs: MirrorConnectorConfig, MirrorSourceConfig, MirrorHeartbeatConfig, MirrorCheckpointConfig
- Server configs: KafkaConfig (Scala), LogConfig, GroupConfig, RemoteLogManagerConfig
- Supporting configs: TopicConfig, SslConfigs, SaslConfigs, SecurityConfig, KRaftConfigs, QuotaConfig

**Documentation Generators (with main methods):**
- Multiple configuration classes have `main()` methods that call `.toHtml()` to generate HTML documentation
- PredicateDoc and TransformationDoc utilities
- These are invoked by Gradle tasks to auto-generate configuration documentation

**REST API Support:**
- ConfigInfo and ConfigKeyInfo classes expose configuration metadata through REST APIs

The output has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file listings, symbol references, and a comprehensive narrative

\"text\": \"# Kafka Configuration Annotation Pattern Discovery\\n\\nIn Apache Kafka, the configuration management system uses the @ConfigDef and @ConfigKey pattern (though these are classes rather than Java annotations) to provide a declarative way to define and document configuration options. This pattern is extensively used throughout the kafka repository.\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### Core Framework (clients module)\\n\\n**ConfigDef** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java`) is the main class that defines configuration schemas. It contains a nested class **ConfigKey** that represents individual configuration parameters with properties like name, type, default value, validator, importance, documentation, group, and display information.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java`) is the base class that all concrete configuration classes extend. It provides methods for parsing and accessing configuration values using a ConfigDef schema.\\n\\n### Configuration Classes Using the Pattern\\n\\nThe ConfigDef/ConfigKey pattern is used extensively throughout Kafka:\\n\\n**Client Configurations:**\\n- `ConsumerConfig` - Kafka consumer configuration options\\n- `ProducerConfig` - Kafka producer configuration options\\n- `AdminClientConfig` - Admin client configuration with main method generating HTML documentation\\n\\n**Streams Configurations:**\\n- `StreamsConfig` - Kafka Streams configuration options with toHtml() documentation generator\\n- `TopologyConfig` - Topology-specific configuration options\\n\\n**Connect Configurations:**\\n- `ConnectorConfig` - Base configuration for all connectors\\n- `SinkConnectorConfig` - Sink connector configuration with main method\\n- `SourceConnectorConfig` - Source connector configuration with main method\\n- `WorkerConfig` - Connect worker configuration\\n- `TaskConfig` - Task configuration\\n- `ConverterConfig` - Base converter configuration\\n- `JsonConverterConfig` - JSON converter configuration\\n- `StringConverterConfig` - String converter configuration\\n- `RestServerConfig` - REST server configuration\\n- `DistributedConfig` - Distributed Connect configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorConnectorConfig` - Mirror connector base configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorSourceConfig` - Mirror source connector configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorHeartbeatConfig` - Mirror heartbeat configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorCheckpointConfig` - Mirror checkpoint configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorClientConfig` - Mirror client configuration\\n\\n**Server/Broker Configurations:**\\n- `KafkaConfig` (Scala) - Broker configuration with main method generating HTML documentation\\n- `LogConfig` - Topic/log configuration with main method\\n- `GroupConfig` - Group coordinator configuration with main method\\n- `RemoteLogManagerConfig` - Remote log manager configuration with main method\\n- `TopicBasedRemoteLogMetadataManagerConfig` - Remote log metadata manager configuration with main method\\n- `ClientMetricsConfigs` - Client metrics configuration\\n\\n**Supporting Configuration Classes:**\\n- `TopicConfig` - Topic-level configuration constants\\n- `SslConfigs` - SSL/TLS configuration constants\\n- `SaslConfigs` - SASL configuration constants\\n- `SecurityConfig` - Security configuration\\n- `KRaftConfigs` - KRaft mode configuration\\n- `QuotaConfig` - Quota configuration\\n\\n### Documentation Generation Chain\\n\\nThe ConfigDef class provides a `toHtml()` method that generates HTML documentation from the configuration schema. Configuration classes implement a `main()` method that uses this functionality to generate documentation:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** - Generates HTML documentation for predicates\\n- **TransformationDoc** - Generates HTML documentation for transformations\\n\\nMany configuration classes have `main()` methods that call `configDef().toHtml()` to generate documentation. These are invoked by Gradle build tasks (seen in build.gradle):\\n- `genKafkaConfigDocs` - generates kafka_config.html\\n- `genTopicConfigDocs` - generates topic_config.html\\n- `genGroupConfigDocs` - generates group_config.html\\n\\n### REST API Layer\\n\\nFor Connect REST APIs, configuration information is exposed through:\\n- `ConfigInfo` - Contains configuration definition and values\\n- `ConfigKeyInfo` - Represents configuration key metadata used in REST responses\\n\\n### Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**AbstractHerder** (`connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java`) contains the `convertConfigKey()` method that transforms ConfigKey objects into ConfigKeyInfo for REST API responses.\\n\\n**KafkaConfigSchema** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/KafkaConfigSchema.java`) provides schema validation utilities that work with ConfigDef objects.\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe ConfigDef/ConfigKey pattern provides a unified, declarative approach to configuration management throughout Apache Kafka. It enables:\\n1. Type-safe configuration definition with validation\\n2. Automatic documentation generation\\n3. Configuration schema introspection\\n4. REST API exposure of configuration metadata\\n5. Consistent handling across all components (brokers, clients, streams, connect)\\n\\nThis pattern is fundamental to Kafka's extensibility and manageability across its diverse ecosystem of components.\"\n}\n",

\"text\": \"# Kafka Configuration Annotation Pattern Discovery\\n\\nIn Apache Kafka, the configuration management system uses the @ConfigDef and @ConfigKey pattern (though these are classes rather than Java annotations) to provide a declarative way to define and document configuration options. This pattern is extensively used throughout the kafka repository.\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### Core Framework (clients module)\\n\\n**ConfigDef** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java`) is the main class that defines configuration schemas. It contains a nested class **ConfigKey** that represents individual configuration parameters with properties like name, type, default value, validator, importance, documentation, group, and display information.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java`) is the base class that all concrete configuration classes extend. It provides methods for parsing and accessing configuration values using a ConfigDef schema.\\n\\n### Configuration Classes Using the Pattern\\n\\nThe ConfigDef/ConfigKey pattern is used extensively throughout Kafka:\\n\\n**Client Configurations:**\\n- `ConsumerConfig` - Kafka consumer configuration options\\n- `ProducerConfig` - Kafka producer configuration options\\n- `AdminClientConfig` - Admin client configuration with main method generating HTML documentation\\n\\n**Streams Configurations:**\\n- `StreamsConfig` - Kafka Streams configuration options with toHtml() documentation generator\\n- `TopologyConfig` - Topology-specific configuration options\\n\\n**Connect Configurations:**\\n- `ConnectorConfig` - Base configuration for all connectors\\n- `SinkConnectorConfig` - Sink connector configuration with main method\\n- `SourceConnectorConfig` - Source connector configuration with main method\\n- `WorkerConfig` - Connect worker configuration\\n- `TaskConfig` - Task configuration\\n- `ConverterConfig` - Base converter configuration\\n- `JsonConverterConfig` - JSON converter configuration\\n- `StringConverterConfig` - String converter configuration\\n- `RestServerConfig` - REST server configuration\\n- `DistributedConfig` - Distributed Connect configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorConnectorConfig` - Mirror connector base configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorSourceConfig` - Mirror source connector configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorHeartbeatConfig` - Mirror heartbeat configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorCheckpointConfig` - Mirror checkpoint configuration with main method\\n- `MirrorClientConfig` - Mirror client configuration\\n\\n**Server/Broker Configurations:**\\n- `KafkaConfig` (Scala) - Broker configuration with main method generating HTML documentation\\n- `LogConfig` - Topic/log configuration with main method\\n- `GroupConfig` - Group coordinator configuration with main method\\n- `RemoteLogManagerConfig` - Remote log manager configuration with main method\\n- `TopicBasedRemoteLogMetadataManagerConfig` - Remote log metadata manager configuration with main method\\n- `ClientMetricsConfigs` - Client metrics configuration\\n\\n**Supporting Configuration Classes:**\\n- `TopicConfig` - Topic-level configuration constants\\n- `SslConfigs` - SSL/TLS configuration constants\\n- `SaslConfigs` - SASL configuration constants\\n- `SecurityConfig` - Security configuration\\n- `KRaftConfigs` - KRaft mode configuration\\n- `QuotaConfig` - Quota configuration\\n\\n### Documentation Generation Chain\\n\\nThe ConfigDef class provides a `toHtml()` method that generates HTML documentation from the configuration schema. Configuration classes implement a `main()` method that uses this functionality to generate documentation:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** - Generates HTML documentation for predicates\\n- **TransformationDoc** - Generates HTML documentation for transformations\\n\\nMany configuration classes have `main()` methods that call `configDef().toHtml()` to generate documentation. These are invoked by Gradle build tasks (seen in build.gradle):\\n- `genKafkaConfigDocs` - generates kafka_config.html\\n- `genTopicConfigDocs` - generates topic_config.html\\n- `genGroupConfigDocs` - generates group_config.html\\n\\n### REST API Layer\\n\\nFor Connect REST APIs, configuration information is exposed through:\\n- `ConfigInfo` - Contains configuration definition and values\\n- `ConfigKeyInfo` - Represents configuration key metadata used in REST responses\\n\\n### Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**AbstractHerder** (`connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java`) contains the `convertConfigKey()` method that transforms ConfigKey objects into ConfigKeyInfo for REST API responses.\\n\\n**KafkaConfigSchema** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/KafkaConfigSchema.java`) provides schema validation utilities that work with ConfigDef objects.\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe ConfigDef/ConfigKey pattern provides a unified, declarative approach to configuration management throughout Apache Kafka. It enables:\\n1. Type-safe configuration definition with validation\\n2. Automatic documentation generation\\n3. Configuration schema introspection\\n4. REST API exposure of configuration metadata\\n5. Consistent handling across all components (brokers, clients, streams, connect)\\n\\nThis pattern is fundamental to Kafka's extensibility and manageability across its diverse ecosystem of components.\"\n}\n",
